Whitney anukramaс╣З─л

[B1. (vss. 25-35). K─Бu┼Ыika.тАФek─Бda┼Ыa. viс╣гс╣Зukramadevaty─Б uta pratimantroktadevaty─Бс╕е. 25-35. 3-av. 6-p. yath─Бkс╣гaraс╣Б ┼Ыakvaryati┼Ыatvar─л.]

Whitney

Comment

тМКThe hymn is mingled prose and verse: 22-24, 42-43, 45-50, and parts of 7-14 and 36-41 are metrical. Cf. Whitney, Index, p. 5.тМЛ This hymn, which by the mss. is given and numbered as one,* without any intimation of a subdivision, is by the Anukr. divided into fourтАа parts, which are even ascribed to different authors. тМКPart A = verses 1-24; B = 25-35; C = 37-41; D = 42-50.тМЛ Verses 1-41, or the first three divisions, are found also in P─Бipp. xvi.; part of the last division (vss. 45, 42 c, d, 43, 44, in this order), in P─Бipp. i.тАФтМК“Water-thunderbolts” appears to me to be nothing more than a highfalutin name, well befitting the black magic of this hymn, for handfuls of water hurled with much hocus-pocus.тМЛ

*тМКBp. does indeed begin anew at vs. 41 (not vs. 42!) to number the verses as 1 etc.тМЛ

тАатМКJust where vs. 36 belongsтАФif it does not form a division by itselfтАФis not clear; it goes well as an ending to the group of vss. 25-35 and is cited with them (Ke┼Ыava, p. 35231: iti dv─Бda┼Ыabhiс╕е). On the other hand, the Anukr. expressly defines division B as ek─Бda┼Ыa; and the corrupt m─Бrtv─л or m─Бrtvi of the Anukr. seems to contain an ascription of authorship for vs. 36. Dr. Ryder suggests that M─Бr─лca may be intended (cf. vii. 62, 63; x. 10). See my arrangement of the Anukr. extracts just before vs. 25.тМЛ

Griffith

A charm to overthrow a rival and gain strength, dignity, long life, children, and general prosperity

режрез рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдпреМрдЬ рд╕реНрдереЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Indra’s force are ye; Indra’s power are ye; Indra’s strength are ye;
    Indra’s heroism are ye; Indra’s manliness are ye; unto a conquering
    junction (y├│ga) with brahman-junctions I join you.
Notes

The pada-text marks a p─Бda-division after each stha; but the Anukr.
lumps all тМКup to the avas─Бna-markтМЛ together as an abhikс╣Ыti-p─Бda (25
syll.), and reckons the whole verse (25: 6 + 8 = 39) mechanically as 2l
pan╠Дkti, because it contains nearly 40 syllables. Ppp. has in
succession balam, nс╣Ыmс╣Зam, ┼Ыuklam, v─лryam, and in c, indrayog─Бis.

тМКRender: ‘for a use conducive to victory, with uses of incantation
[or with masterly uses] [or with Brahman uses] I use you.’ In
brahma- I am inclined to see a triple ┼Ыleс╣гa, the second sense being
like that in the title Brahma-j─Бla-sutta (of the D─лghanik─Бya), ’the
boss-net, the master-net.’ In the first and second senses, brahma- is
pertinent: not so in the sense of Brahman, in which last, however, it
serves well enough for a point of departure for kс╣гatram, considering
what black magic this is.тМЛ

Griffith

Ye are the power of Indra, ye the force and strength of Indra, ye his hero might and manliness. I join you with the bonds of Prayer to the victorious enterprise.

Notes

In these verses, P─Бipp. makes 9 and 10, also 11 and 12, change places.
After our 13 it inserts two more verses, beginning bс╣Ыhaspater and
praj─Бpater; and in our 14 it omits devasya, and reads ┼Ыuklaс╣Б dev─лr
─Бpo. To read dhattana for dhatta тМКand pronounce dh─Б╠Бman─Б would
make a regular anuс╣гс╣нubh of the refrain. The Anukr., as usual, gives no
real description of the agglomeration, but calls 11 and 14 pan╠Дkti
because they count up 40 syllables (9: 8 + 7: 8 + 8 = 40), and the
others bс╣Ыhat─л because they have nearly 36 syllables. As to the alleged
quotation of vs. 7 in K─Бu┼Ы. 49. 25, see above, note to vs. 6.

резрел рдпреЛ рд╡ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. What of you, O waters, is the portion of waters within the waters,
    of the nature of sacrificial formula, sacrificing to the gods, that now
    I let go; that let me not wash down against myself; that do we let go
    against him who hates us, whom we hate; him may I slay (vadh), him may
    I lay low, with this spell (br├бhman), with this act, with this weapon
    (men├н).
Notes

тМКRender c: ’therewith (i.e. ap─Бm bh─Бgena = udavajreс╣Зa) do we let
fly against (abhyati-sс╣Ыj) him or do we shoot against him who’ etc.;
i.e. ati-sс╣Ыj is used intransitively and “him” is governed by the
abhi-.тМЛ тМКP─Бdas b, c are repeated below as xvi. 1. 4, 5.тМЛ At the
beginning of c read t├йna (accent-sign slipped out of place).

Griffith

Waters, your ceremonial share of Waters which the waters hold, which aids our sacrifice to Gods, This as a remnant here I leave. Do not thou wash it clean away. With this we let the man go by who hates us and whom we abhor. Him would I fain o’erthrow and slay with this our ceremonial act, with this our prayer, our thunder-bolt.

Whitney
Translation
  1. What of you, O waters, are the fires of the waters within the
    waters, of the nature of sacrificial formula, sacrificing to the gods,
    them now I let go; them let me not wash down against myself; them we let
    go against him who hates us, etc. etc.

garbho respectively. For the quotations in K─Бu┼Ы. of the common

introductionтМЛ. In all the verses it is possible only by violence to make

Griffith

Whatever evil I have done within this last triennium, From all that woe and misery let the waters shield and guard me well.

Whitney
Translation
  1. I send you forth to the ocean; go ye unto your own lair; uninjured,
    of completed years (?); and let nothing whatever ail (am) us.
Notes

Griffith

Onward I urge your gathered floods: enter your own abiding- place, Uninjured and with all your strength. Let nothing bend or bow us down.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Free from defilement (-ripr├б) [are] the waters; [let them
    carry] away from us defilement, forth from us sin, mishap (durit├б),
    they of good aspect; let them carry forth evil dreaming, forth filth.
Notes

The verse is in part repeated below, as xvi. 1. 10, 11.

[B┬╣. (vss. 25-35). K─Бu┼Ыika.тАФek─Бda┼Ыa. viс╣гс╣Зukramadevaty─Б uta
pratimantroktadevaty─Бс╕е. 25-35. 3-av. 6-p. yath─Бkс╣гaraс╣Б
┼Ыakvaryati┼Ыatvar─л.]

[B┬▓. (vs. 36). M─Бrtv─л (?).тАФ5-p. ati┼Ы─Бkvar─Бtij─Бgatagarbh─Б тАЩс╣гс╣нi. See
introduction.]

Griffith

May the pure Waters cleanse us from defilement, Fair to behold remove our sin and trouble, and bear away ill- dream and all pollution.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Vishс╣Зu’s stride art thou, rival-slaying, earth-sharpened
    (-s├бс╣Б┼Ыita), Agni-brightened; after earth I stride out; from earth we
    disportion him who hates us, whom we hate; let him not live; him let
    breath quit.
Notes

The P─Бipp. version of sections B. and C. agrees with that of our text
with only trifling differences; the details are not furnished. It is not
difficult to read this and the following verses of B. into ┼Ыakvar─л and
ati┼Ыakvar─л verses, as required by the Anukr. (this, for example, as 10

  • 10: 9 + 8: 9 + 10 = 56). The whole section, apparently, is quoted by
    its common prat─лka in K─Бu┼Ы. 6. 14, to accompany the taking of the
    Viс╣гс╣Зu strides in a parvan ceremony; and again in 49. 14 тМКafter hurling
    the water-bolts: cf. introd.тМЛ. тМКCf. vii. 31. 1 d.тМЛ
Griffith

Thou art the step of Vishnu, rival-slayer, sharpened by earth, aglow with fire of Agni, Earth have I ranged: from earth we bar him who hates us and whom we hate.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Vishс╣Зu’s stride art thou, rival-slaying, atmosphere-sharpened,
    Vayu-brightened; after atmosphere I stride out; from atmosphere we
    disportion him who etc. etc.
Notes
Griffith

Ours is superior place and ours is conquest: may I in all fights tread down spite and malice. Let him not live, let vital breath desert him.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Ours [is] what is conquered, ours what has shot up; I have
    withstood (abhi-sth─Б) all fighters, niggards; now do I involve
    (ni-veс╣гс╣н) the splendor, brightness, breath, life-time of him of
    such-and-such lineage, son of such-and-such mother; now do I make him
    fall (pad) downward.
Notes

тМКAs to the place of this vs. in the general divisions of the hymn and
its possible ascription to M─Бr─лca, see the introd. and the Anukr.
excerpts above.тМЛ With this vs. compare xvi. 8. 1; тМКalso the mantra
cited at K─Бu┼Ы. 47. 22тМЛ. The vs. reads naturally as 62 syllables (11 +
11: 15 + 13 + 12 = 62), but can be brought by forced resolutions up to a
full aс╣гс╣нi (64 syll.). Abhy aс╣гс╣нh─Бm is by Pr─Бt. ii. 92.

[C. (vss. 37-41). Brahman.тАФpa├▒ca. pratimantroktadevaty─Бс╕е. 37. vir─Бс╣н
purast─Бdbс╣Ыhat─л; 38. pur─Бuс╣гс╣Зih; 39, 41. ─Бrс╣г─л g─Бyatr─л; 40. vir─Бс╕Н viс╣гam─Б
g─Бyatr─л.]

Griffith

With this I here invest the power and splendour, the life of that man and his vital breathing, the son of such a sire and such a woman, here do I overthrow and cast him downward.

Whitney
Translation
  1. I turn after the sun’s turn (─Бvс╣Ы╠Бt), after his turn to the right;
    let it yield (yam) me property; [let] it [yield] me
    Brahman-splendor.
Notes

The verse is quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 6. 15, in a parvan ceremony, accompanying
a turn to the right (vss. 25-35 were quoted in the next preceding rule).
тМКCf. also MB. i. 6. 19, where the comm. cites also GGS. ii. 10. 27.тМЛ

Griffith

I follow Surya’s course in heaven, the course that takes him to the South. May that bestow upon me wealth and glory of a Brahman’s rank.

рекрек рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдЮреЛ рд╡рд░реБрдгрд╕реНрдп ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. King Varuс╣Зa’s bond art thou; do thou bind so-and-so, of
    such-and-such lineage, son of such-and-such mother, in food, in breath.
Notes

There is apparently something wrong, perhaps an omission, in the text of
the Anukr. at this point; it reads trip─Бd g─Бyatragarbh─Б st anuс╣гс╣нubh,
and then passes to vs. 50, taking no notice of vss. 48, 49 (which are
redundant triс╣гс╣нubhs: but see the note to vs. 49), тМКnor of vs. 47тМЛ. Our
present verse (prose) reads most naturally as 10: 12 + 7 = 29 syllables.

Griffith

Thou art the bound of Varuna the King. Bind, such an one, the son of such a woman, in vital breath and in the food that feeds him.

Translation
  1. What food of thine, O Lord of earth (bh┼л╠Б), dwells upon the earth
    (pс╣Ыthiv─л╠Б)тАФof that, O lord of earth, do thou furnish unto us, O
    Praj─Бpati.
Notes

The Anukr. implies the contraction of с╣гiyati in b to kс╣гyati (cf.
above, 2. 22, 23). Ppp. тМКin i.тМЛ puts this verse before our vs. 42.

Griffith

All food of thine, O Lord of Life, that lies, upon the face of earth, Thereof bestow thou upon us. O Lord of Life, Prajapati!

Translation
  1. The heavenly waters have I honored; with sap have we been mingled;

Griffith

Celestial Waters have I sought: with juice have I besprinkled them. With milk, O Agni, have I come; bestow upon me splendid strength.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Unite me, O Agni, with splendor, with progeny, with life-time; may
    the gods know me as such; may Indra know, together with the seers.
Notes

These two verses we had above, as vii. 89. 1, 2. Neither they nor the
two that follow are found in Ppp. here.

Griffith

Give me the boon of splendid strength; give, Agni! progeny and life. May the Gods know this prayer of mine, may Indra with the Rishis know.

Translation
  1. Crush away the sorcerers with heat; crush away, O Agni, the demon
    with flame; crush away with burning the false worshipers; crush away the
    greatly gleaming ones that feed on lives.
Notes

These two verses are viii. 3. 12, 13. As usual in such a case, only the
first words are given here in the mss. (both pada and saс╣Бhit─Б):
thus, y├бd agna ├нti dv├й. Unfortunately it was overlooked by us that
y├бd agne begins not only viii. 3. 12, but also vii. 61. 1; and, though
both passages fit about equally ill into the connection here, yet the
meter of vii. 61. 1, 2, being anuс╣гс╣нubh, implies a less oversight on
the part of the Anukr., and, on the whole, the chance is in favor of the
latter passage (vii. 61. 1, 2) being the one here intended. If in any
one of the mss. accessible to us since the publication of the text there
occurs anything to settle the question, it has been overlooked by us.
тМКSPP. fills out the prat─лka with viii. 3. 12, 13; but herein he may
merely have followed the Berlin edition.тМЛ

Griffith

Destroy the Yatudhanas with thy fervour, consume the demons with thy wrath, O Agni. Destroy the fool’s gods with thy fiery splendour, destroy the blazing ones, the insatiable.

Whitney
Translation
  1. I, knowing, hurl at this man, to split his head, the four-pointed
    (-bhс╣Ыс╣гс╣н├н) thunderbolt of the waters; let it crush all his limbs: to
    this on my part let all the gods assent.

a. For the quotations of the verse, with other verses of the hymn,
by K─Бu┼Ы., see above тМКintroductionтМЛ.

Griffith

Well-skilled, against this man I hurl the Water’s bolt with four spikes, to cleave his head asunder. May it destroy all members of his body. Let the whole host of Gods approve my purpose.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдореИрдВ (рдЕрд╕реНрдореИ) рдЗрд╕ [рд╢рддреНрд░реБ рдкрд░] (рд╢реАрд░реНрд╖рднрд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдп) рд╢рд┐рд░ рддреЛрдбрд╝рдиреЗ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рдЕрдкрд╛рдореН) рдЬрд▓реЛрдВ рдХрд╛ (рдЪрддреБрд░реНрднреГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдореН) рдЪреМрдлрд╛рд▓реЗ (рд╡рдЬреНрд░рдореН) рд╡рдЬреНрд░ [рдЕрд╕реНрддреНрд░] рдХреЛ (рдкреНрд░ рд╣рд░рд╛рдорд┐) рдЪрд▓рд╛рддрд╛ рд╣реВрдБред (рд╕рдГ) рд╡рд╣ [рд╡рдЬреНрд░] (рдЕрд╕реНрдп) рдЙрд╕ рдХреЗ (рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛) рд╕рдм (рдЕрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирд┐) рдЕрдЩреНрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рдкреНрд░ рд╢реГрдгрд╛рддреБ) рдЪреВрд░-рдЪреВрд░ рдХрд░ рдбрд╛рд▓реЗ, (рдореЗ) рдореЗрд░реЗ (рддрддреН) рдЙрд╕ [рдХрд░реНрдо] рдХреЛ (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗ) рд╕рдм (рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд▓реЛрдЧ (рдЕрдиреБ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреНрддреБ) рдорд╛рди рд▓реЗрд╡реЗрдВ реерелрежрее
